      <p><b>Afghanistan</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'f' in 'find'">f</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/ɡ/: 'g' in 'guy'">ɡ</span><span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span></span>,<span class="wrap"> </span><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'f' in 'find'">f</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/ɡ/: 'g' in 'guy'">ɡ</span><span title="/ɑː/: 'a' in 'father'">ɑː</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/ɑː/: 'a' in 'father'">ɑː</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Afghanistan.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/ff/En-us-Afghanistan.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Afghanistan.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>, also pronounced /<span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">ævˈɡænᵻstæn, ævˈɡɑːnᵻstɑːn</span>/;<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[10]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pashto" class="mw-redirect" title="Pashto">Pashto</a>/<a href="/wiki/Dari_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Dari language">Dari</a>: <span lang="ps" dir="rtl" title="Pashto language text">افغانستان</span>, Pashto: <i lang="ps-Latn" title="Pashto language text">Afġānistān</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" class="mw-redirect" title="Help:IPA">[avɣɒnisˈtɒn, ab-]</a></span>, Dari: <i lang="prs-Latn" title="Dari language text">Afġānestān</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Help:IPA/Persian&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Help:IPA/Persian (not yet started)">[avɣɒnesˈtɒn]</a></span>), officially the <b>Islamic Republic of Afghanistan</b>, is a <a href="/wiki/Country" title="Country">country</a> located in <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cia_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-13">[12]</a></sup> It has borders with <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> in the south and east, <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> in the west, <a href="/wiki/Turkmenistan" title="Turkmenistan">Turkmenistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uzbekistan" title="Uzbekistan">Uzbekistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tajikistan" title="Tajikistan">Tajikistan</a> in the north, and <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> in the far northeast.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-13">[12]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In early times people passed through it with animals and other goods as it connected China and India with <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a> and the Middle East. More recently, Afghanistan has been damaged by many years of war. This has resulted in there not being enough jobs. </p>
      <p>The country is around 251,826 square miles (652,230 square kilometres) in size or area. There are 30 million people in Afghanistan. There are about 3 million Afghan <a href="/wiki/Refugees" class="mw-redirect" title="Refugees">refugees</a> (people who had to leave the country) who are in Pakistan and Iran for some time. In 2011, its capital, <a href="/wiki/Kabul" title="Kabul">Kabul</a>, had about 3,691,400 people living in it.<sup id="cite_ref-cso.gov.af_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cso.gov.af-14">[13]</a></sup> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afghanistan&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=1" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Geography">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afghanistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Change section: Geography">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Black_Hawk_flying_over_a_valley_in_Bamyan.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Black_Hawk_flying_over_a_valley_in_Bamyan.jpg/220px-Black_Hawk_flying_over_a_valley_in_Bamyan.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Black_Hawk_flying_over_a_valley_in_Bamyan.jpg/330px-Black_Hawk_flying_over_a_valley_in_Bamyan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Black_Hawk_flying_over_a_valley_in_Bamyan.jpg/440px-Black_Hawk_flying_over_a_valley_in_Bamyan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Black_Hawk_flying_over_a_valley_in_Bamyan.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Snow-capped Koh-i-Baba mountains in <a href="/wiki/Bamyan_Province" title="Bamyan Province">Bamyan Province</a> of Afghanistan.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Afghanistan has many <a href="/wiki/Mountains" class="mw-redirect" title="Mountains">mountains</a>. The mountains are called the <a href="/wiki/Hindu_Kush" title="Hindu Kush">Hindu Kush</a> and <a href="/wiki/Himalayas" title="Himalayas">Himalayas</a>. The big mountain in Afghanistan is <a href="/wiki/Noshaq" title="Noshaq">Mount Nowshak</a>. There are <a href="/wiki/Plains" class="mw-redirect" title="Plains">plains</a> (which have soil that is good for growing plants) and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Foothills&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Foothills (not yet started)">foothills</a>. Part is also dry and called the <a href="/wiki/Registan_Desert" title="Registan Desert">Registan Desert</a>. </p>
      <p>Afghanistan has snow and <a href="/wiki/Glaciers" class="mw-redirect" title="Glaciers">glaciers</a> in the mountains. <a href="/wiki/Amu_Darya" title="Amu Darya">Amu Darya</a> is the big water stream, or river. </p>
      <p>The country has a lot of a <a href="/w/index.php?title=Valuable&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Valuable (not yet started)">valuable</a> <a href="/wiki/Stone" title="Stone">stone</a> called <a href="/wiki/Lapis_lazuli" title="Lapis lazuli">lapis lazuli</a>, which was used to decorate the <a href="/wiki/Tomb" title="Tomb">tomb</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egyptian</a> king <a href="/wiki/Tutankhamun" title="Tutankhamun">Tutankhamun</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ngk_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ngk-15">[14]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afghanistan&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=2" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Climate">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afghanistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Change section: Climate">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Afghanistan has a <a href="/wiki/Continental_climate" title="Continental climate">continental climate</a> with hot summers and cold winters. Having no water sometimes causes problems for <a href="/wiki/Farmers" class="mw-redirect" title="Farmers">farmers</a>. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Sandstorms&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Sandstorms (not yet started)">Sandstorms</a> happen a lot in the <a href="/wiki/Desert" title="Desert">desert</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Plants_and_animals">Plants and animals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afghanistan&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=3" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Plants and animals">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afghanistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Change section: Plants and animals">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Uncia_uncia_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Uncia_uncia_2.jpg/150px-Uncia_uncia_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="100" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Uncia_uncia_2.jpg/225px-Uncia_uncia_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Uncia_uncia_2.jpg/300px-Uncia_uncia_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="467"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Uncia_uncia_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Endangered <a href="/wiki/Snow_leopard" title="Snow leopard">snow leopards</a> live in the cold <a href="/wiki/Hindu_Kush" title="Hindu Kush">Hindu Kush</a>, but they have thick <a href="/wiki/Fur" title="Fur">fur</a> to stay warm. Hunters sell the soft leopard skins in the markets in the capital <a href="/wiki/Kabul" title="Kabul">Kabul</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/South" title="South">Southern</a> Afghanistan has not many plants because it is dry. There are more plants where there is more water. Mountains have <a href="/wiki/Forests" class="mw-redirect" title="Forests">forests</a> of <a href="/wiki/Pine" title="Pine">pine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fir" title="Fir">fir</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cedar" title="Cedar">cedar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oak" title="Oak">oak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Walnut" title="Walnut">walnut</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alder" title="Alder">alder</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ash_tree" title="Ash tree">ash trees</a>. </p>
      <p>Afghanistan's wild animals live in the mountains. There are <a href="/wiki/Wolves" class="mw-redirect" title="Wolves">wolves</a>, <a href="/wiki/Foxes" class="mw-redirect" title="Foxes">foxes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jackals" class="mw-redirect" title="Jackals">jackals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bears" class="mw-redirect" title="Bears">bears</a>, and wild <a href="/wiki/Goat" class="mw-redirect" title="Goat">goats</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gazelle" title="Gazelle">gazelles</a>, wild dogs, <a href="/wiki/Camel" title="Camel">camels</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wild_cat" class="mw-redirect" title="Wild cat">wild cats</a> such as the <a href="/wiki/Snow_leopard" title="Snow leopard">snow leopard</a> in the country. The birds are <a href="/wiki/Falcon" title="Falcon">falcons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eagles" class="mw-redirect" title="Eagles">eagles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vulture" title="Vulture">vultures</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Rhesus_Macaque" class="mw-redirect" title="Rhesus Macaque">Rhesus Macaque</a> and the red flying <a href="/wiki/Squirrel" title="Squirrel">squirrel</a> are also in Afghanistan. </p>
      <p>Many years of <a href="/wiki/War" title="War">war</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hunting" title="Hunting">hunting</a>, and years of no water have killed animals in Afghanistan. There used to be <a href="/wiki/Tigers" class="mw-redirect" title="Tigers">tigers</a> in Afghanistan, but now there aren't any. Bears and wolves are almost gone.<sup id="cite_ref-ngk_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ngk-15">[14]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="People_and_culture">People and culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afghanistan&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=4" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: People and culture">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afghanistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Change section: People and culture">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:2011_Afghan_Youth_Voices_Festival.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/2011_Afghan_Youth_Voices_Festival.jpg/220px-2011_Afghan_Youth_Voices_Festival.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/2011_Afghan_Youth_Voices_Festival.jpg/330px-2011_Afghan_Youth_Voices_Festival.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/2011_Afghan_Youth_Voices_Festival.jpg/440px-2011_Afghan_Youth_Voices_Festival.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:2011_Afghan_Youth_Voices_Festival.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The 2011 Afghan Youth Voices Festival at the Gardens of Babur in <a href="/wiki/Kabul" title="Kabul">Kabul</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Many people have moved through or invaded the land of Afghanistan. Today's people of Afghanistan are known as <i>Afghans</i>. They have many traits passed down from these previous peoples. </p>
      <p>The largest <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_group" title="Ethnic group">group</a> of people are the <a href="/wiki/Pashtun_people" title="Pashtun people">Pashtuns</a>. These make up about half the population.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[16]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tajik_people" title="Tajik people">Tajiks</a> are the second-largest ethnic group, making up about one-fifth of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-Brit-Tajik_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brit-Tajik-18">[17]</a></sup> Before the 20th century, Tajiks were called Sarts<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup> and some come from the Iranian peoples.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[19]</a></sup> Most Pashtuns are also related to the Iranian peoples. Some Pashtuns and Tajiks marry each other but at the same time they are rivals. The third-largest group are the <a href="/wiki/Hazara_people" title="Hazara people">Hazaras</a>. They are native to the <a href="/wiki/Hazaristan" title="Hazaristan">Hazaristan</a> area in central Afghanistan. The country's other groups include the <a href="/wiki/Uzbek_people" title="Uzbek people">Uzbek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aimaq_people" title="Aimaq people">Aimaq</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkmen_people" title="Turkmen people">Turkmen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nuristani_people" title="Nuristani people">Nuristani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baloch_people" title="Baloch people">Baloch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pashayi_people" title="Pashayi people">Pashayi</a> and a few others.<sup id="cite_ref-ngk_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ngk-15">[14]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Dari-Persian and Pashto are the official languages of Afghanistan. Many people speak both languages.<sup id="cite_ref-AO_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AO-1">[1]</a></sup> Both are <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Indo-European language">Indo-European languages</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Iranian_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Iranian languages">Iranian languages</a> sub-family. They are usually written with the <a href="/wiki/Arabic_alphabet" title="Arabic alphabet">Arabic alphabet</a>. <a href="/wiki/Uzbek_language" title="Uzbek language">Uzbek</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turkmen_language" title="Turkmen language">Turkmen</a> are widely spoken in the north and <a href="/wiki/Nuristani_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuristani language">Nuristani</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pashai_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Pashai language">Pashai</a> are spoken in the east.<sup id="cite_ref-AO_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AO-1">[1]</a></sup> Almost all Afghans follow the religion of <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>. </p>
      <p>Afghanistan is a largely <a href="/wiki/Rural" class="mw-redirect" title="Rural">rural</a> country. This means there are only a few major cities. About one fifth of the population live in cities. <a href="/wiki/Kabul" title="Kabul">Kabul</a>, the capital, is the largest city. It is south of the <a href="/wiki/Hindu_Kush" title="Hindu Kush">Hindu Kush</a> range and alongside the <a href="/wiki/Kabul_River" title="Kabul River">Kabul River</a>. Other cities in Afghanistan include <a href="/wiki/Kandahar" title="Kandahar">Kandahar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Herat" title="Herat">Herat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mazar-e_Sharif" class="mw-redirect" title="Mazar-e Sharif">Mazar-e Sharif</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jalalabad" title="Jalalabad">Jalalabad</a>. The rural population is made up of <a href="/wiki/Farmer" title="Farmer">farmers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nomad" class="mw-redirect" title="Nomad">nomads</a>. The farmers live mainly in small villages along the rivers. The nomads live in tents while moving from place to place with their animals and belongings. Some people live in the high central mountains. Some live in the deserts in the south and southwest. Millions of people left Afghanistan to get away from the wars that happened in the late 20th and early 21st centuries. Most of them lived in neighboring <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afghanistan&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=5" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: History">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afghanistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Change section: History">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>Afghanistan is in the <a href="/wiki/Trail" title="Trail">path</a> of important trade routes that connect southern and eastern <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a> to <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a>. Because of this, many empire builders have decided to rule over the area. Signs that these emperors were near Afghanistan still exist in many parts of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[20]</a></sup> Afghanistan is near what used to be the <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a>, so it has many cultures. From up to 8,000 years ago, the peoples of Afghanistan helped develop (create) major world religions, traded and exchanged many <a href="/wiki/Product_(business)" title="Product (business)">products</a>, and sometimes controlled politics and culture in Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[21]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">Prehistory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afghanistan&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=6" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Prehistory">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afghanistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Change section: Prehistory">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Raffael_071.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Raffael_071.jpg/170px-Raffael_071.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="100" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Raffael_071.jpg/255px-Raffael_071.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Raffael_071.jpg/340px-Raffael_071.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1205"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Raffael_071.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Zoroaster" title="Zoroaster">Zoroaster</a>, the founder of <a href="/wiki/Zoroastrianism" title="Zoroastrianism">Zoroastrianism</a>, lived in <a href="/wiki/Bactria" title="Bactria">Bactria</a>, an ancient land in the north of today's Afghanistan.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Archaeology" title="Archaeology">Archaeologists</a> digging a cave in what is now northeastern Afghanistan (in <a href="/wiki/Badakhshan_Province" title="Badakhshan Province">Badakhshan</a>), discovered that people lived in the country as early as 100,000 years ago. They found the skull of a <a href="/wiki/Neanderthal" title="Neanderthal">Neanderthal</a>, or early human, as well as tools from about 30,000 years ago. In other parts of Afghanistan, archaeologists uncovered <a href="/wiki/Pottery" title="Pottery">pottery</a> and tools that are 4,000 to 11,000 years old—evidence that Afghans were among the first people in the world to grow crops and raise animals.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-23">[22]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kaunakes_Bactria_Louvre_AO31917.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Kaunakes_Bactria_Louvre_AO31917.jpg/150px-Kaunakes_Bactria_Louvre_AO31917.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Kaunakes_Bactria_Louvre_AO31917.jpg/225px-Kaunakes_Bactria_Louvre_AO31917.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Kaunakes_Bactria_Louvre_AO31917.jpg/300px-Kaunakes_Bactria_Louvre_AO31917.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1170" data-file-height="1300"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kaunakes_Bactria_Louvre_AO31917.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A Stone Female Figurine, known as <b>Bactrian Princess</b>, from <a href="/wiki/Bactria" title="Bactria">Bactria</a>, north of Afghanistan, about 4,000 years ago
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Farmers and herders settled in the plains surrounding the <a href="/wiki/Hindu_Kush" title="Hindu Kush">Hindu Kush</a> as early as 7000 B.C. These people may have grown rich off the <a href="/wiki/Lapis_lazuli" title="Lapis lazuli">lapis lazuli</a> they found along riverbeds, which they traded to early city sites to the west, across the <a href="/wiki/Iranian_plateau" title="Iranian plateau">Iranian plateau</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a>. As farms and villages grew and thrived in Afghanistan, these ancient people eventually invented <a href="/wiki/Irrigation" title="Irrigation">irrigation</a> (digging ditches for water so it flows to crops) that allowed them to grow crops on the northern Afghanistan desert plains. This <a href="/wiki/Civilization" title="Civilization">civilization</a> (advanced state of organization) is today called BMAC (<a href="/wiki/Bactria%E2%80%93Margiana_Archaeological_Complex" title="Bactria–Margiana Archaeological Complex">Bactria–Margiana Archaeological Complex</a>), or the "Oxus civilization".<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Oxus civilization expanded as far east as western edge of the <a href="/wiki/Indus_Valley" class="mw-redirect" title="Indus Valley">Indus Valley</a> during the period between 2200 and 1800 B.C.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup> These people, who were the ancestors of the Indo-Aryans, used the term "<a href="/wiki/Aryan" title="Aryan">Aryan</a>" to identify their ethnicity, culture, and religion. Scholars know this when they read the ancient texts of these people; the <a href="/wiki/Avesta_(religious_scripture)" class="mw-redirect" title="Avesta (religious scripture)">Avesta</a> of Iranian people and the <a href="/wiki/Vedas" title="Vedas">Vedas</a> of Indo-Aryans.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Zoroaster" title="Zoroaster">Zoroaster</a>, the founder of the <a href="/wiki/Zoroastrian" class="mw-redirect" title="Zoroastrian">Zoroastrian</a> religion, the world's earliest <a href="/wiki/Monotheistic" class="mw-redirect" title="Monotheistic">monotheistic</a> religion, (meaning a religion believing in one god) lived in the area (somewhere north of today's Afghanistan), around 1000 B.C.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient_history">Ancient history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afghanistan&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=7" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Ancient history">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afghanistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Change section: Ancient history">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ancient_Khorasan_highlighted.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Ancient_Khorasan_highlighted.jpg/220px-Ancient_Khorasan_highlighted.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="189" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Ancient_Khorasan_highlighted.jpg/330px-Ancient_Khorasan_highlighted.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/38/Ancient_Khorasan_highlighted.jpg 2x" data-file-width="373" data-file-height="320"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ancient_Khorasan_highlighted.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Names of territories during the <a href="/wiki/Caliphate" title="Caliphate">Caliphate</a> in 750 CE. <a href="/wiki/Greater_Khorasan" title="Greater Khorasan">Khorasan</a> was part of Persia (in <a href="/wiki/Yellow" title="Yellow">yellowish</a>).
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Before the middle of the sixth century <a href="/wiki/BCE" class="mw-redirect" title="BCE">BCE</a>, the land was held by the <a href="/wiki/Medes" title="Medes">Medes</a>. Then the <a href="/wiki/Achaemenids" class="mw-redirect" title="Achaemenids">Achaemenids</a> took over control of the land and made it part of the <a href="/wiki/Persian_empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Persian empire">Persian empire</a>. <a href="/wiki/Alexander_the_great" class="mw-redirect" title="Alexander the great">Alexander the great</a> defeated and conquered the Persian Empire in 330 BCE. He founded some cities in the area. The people used <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">Greek</a> culture and language. After Alexander, <a href="/wiki/Greco-Bactrians" class="mw-redirect" title="Greco-Bactrians">Greco-Bactrians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scythians" title="Scythians">Scythians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kushans" class="mw-redirect" title="Kushans">Kushans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Parthians" class="mw-redirect" title="Parthians">Parthians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sassanians" class="mw-redirect" title="Sassanians">Sassanians</a> ruled the area.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Kushans spread <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> from <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> in the 1st century BCE, and Buddhism remained an important religion in the area until the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_conquest" class="mw-redirect" title="Islamic conquest">Islamic conquest</a> in the 7th century CE.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Buddhas_of_Bamiyan" title="Buddhas of Bamiyan">Buddhas of Bamiyan</a> were giant statues, a reminder of Buddhism in Afghanistan. They were destroyed by the <a href="/wiki/Taliban" title="Taliban">Taliban</a> in 2001. There were international protests. The Taliban believe that the ancient statues were <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">un-Islamic</a> and that they had a right to destroy them. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medieval_history">Medieval history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afghanistan&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=8" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Medieval history">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afghanistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Change section: Medieval history">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Arabs" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabs">Arabs</a> introduced <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> in the 7th century and slowly began spreading the new religion. In the 9th and 10th centuries, many local Islamic dynasties rose to power inside Afghanistan. One of the earliest was the <a href="/wiki/Tahirids" class="mw-redirect" title="Tahirids">Tahirids</a>, whose kingdom included <a href="/wiki/Balkh" title="Balkh">Balkh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Herat" title="Herat">Herat</a>; they established independence from the <a href="/wiki/Abbasids" class="mw-redirect" title="Abbasids">Abbasids</a> in 820. The Tahirids were succeeded in about 867 by the <a href="/wiki/Saffarids" class="mw-redirect" title="Saffarids">Saffarids</a> of <a href="/wiki/Zaranj" title="Zaranj">Zaranj</a> in western Afghanistan. Local princes in the north soon became <a href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/feudatory" class="extiw" title="wikt:feudatory">feudatories</a> of the powerful <a href="/wiki/Samanids" class="mw-redirect" title="Samanids">Samanids</a>, who ruled from <a href="/wiki/Bukhara" title="Bukhara">Bukhara</a>. From 872 to 999, north of the Hindu Kush in Afghanistan enjoyed a golden age under Samanid rule.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the 10th century, the local <a href="/wiki/Ghaznavid_Empire" title="Ghaznavid Empire">Ghaznavids</a> turned <a href="/wiki/Ghazni" title="Ghazni">Ghazni</a> into their capital and firmly established Islam throughout all areas of Afghanistan, except the Kafiristan region in the northeast. <a href="/wiki/Mahmud_of_Ghazni" title="Mahmud of Ghazni">Mahmud of Ghazni</a>, a great Ghaznavid <a href="/wiki/Sultan" title="Sultan">sultan</a>, conquered the <a href="/wiki/Multan" title="Multan">Multan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Punjab_region" title="Punjab region">Punjab region</a>, and carried raids into the heart of <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>. Mohammed bin Abdul Jabbar Utbi (Al-Utbi), a historian from the 10th century, wrote that thousands of "Afghans" were in the Ghaznavid army.<sup id="cite_ref-Houtsma_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Houtsma-32">[31]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Habibi_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Habibi-33">[32]</a></sup> The Ghaznavid dynasty was replaced by the Ghorids of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghor&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ghor (not yet started)">Ghor</a> in the late 12th century, who reconquered Ghaznavid territory in the name of Islam and ruled it until 1206. The Ghorid army also included ethnic Afghans.<sup id="cite_ref-Houtsma_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Houtsma-32">[31]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Portrait_miniature_of_Ahmad_Shah_Durrani.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Portrait_miniature_of_Ahmad_Shah_Durrani.jpg/150px-Portrait_miniature_of_Ahmad_Shah_Durrani.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="202" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Portrait_miniature_of_Ahmad_Shah_Durrani.jpg/225px-Portrait_miniature_of_Ahmad_Shah_Durrani.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Portrait_miniature_of_Ahmad_Shah_Durrani.jpg/300px-Portrait_miniature_of_Ahmad_Shah_Durrani.jpg 2x" data-file-width="933" data-file-height="1259"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Portrait_miniature_of_Ahmad_Shah_Durrani.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Ahmad_Shah_Durrani" title="Ahmad Shah Durrani">Ahmad Shah Durrani</a>, founder of the modern state of Afghanistan in 1747.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Afghanistan was recognized as <i>Khorasan</i>, meaning "land of the rising sun," which was a prosperous and independent geographic region reaching as far as the Indus River.<sup id="cite_ref-EI_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EI-34">[33]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-35">[34]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>All the major cities of modern Afghanistan were centers of science and culture in the past. The New Persian <a href="/wiki/Literature" title="Literature">literature</a> arose and flourished in the area. The early Persian poets such as <a href="/wiki/Rudaki" title="Rudaki">Rudaki</a> were from what is now Afghanistan. Moreover, <a href="/wiki/Ferdowsi" title="Ferdowsi">Ferdowsi</a>, the author of <a href="/wiki/Shahnameh" title="Shahnameh">Shahnameh</a>, the national <a href="/wiki/Epic_poetry" title="Epic poetry">epic</a> of Iran, and <a href="/wiki/Rumi" title="Rumi">Rumi</a>, the famous <a href="/wiki/Sufi" class="mw-redirect" title="Sufi">Sufi</a> poet, were also from modern-day Afghanistan. It has produced scientists such as <a href="/wiki/Avicenna" title="Avicenna">Avicenna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al-Farabi" title="Al-Farabi">Al-Farabi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al-Biruni" class="mw-redirect" title="Al-Biruni">Al-Biruni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Omar_Khayy%C3%A1m" title="Omar Khayyám">Omar Khayyám</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al-Khwarizmi" title="Al-Khwarizmi">Al-Khwarizmi</a>, and many others who are widely known for their important contributions in areas such as <a href="/wiki/Mathematics" title="Mathematics">mathematics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Astronomy" title="Astronomy">astronomy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Medicine" title="Medicine">medicine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">physics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Geography" title="Geography">geography</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Geology" title="Geology">geology</a>. It remained the cultural capital of Persia until the devastating <a href="/wiki/Mongol" class="mw-redirect" title="Mongol">Mongol</a> invasion in the 13th century.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[35]</a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[36]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><br> <a href="/wiki/Timur" class="mw-redirect" title="Timur">Timur</a>, the Turkic conqueror, took over in the end of the 14th century and began to rebuild cities in this region. Timur's successors, the <a href="/wiki/Timurids" class="mw-redirect" title="Timurids">Timurids</a> (1405–1507), were great patrons of learning and the arts who enriched their capital city of Herat with fine buildings. Under their rule Afghanistan enjoyed peace and prosperity. </p>
      <p>Between south of the Hindu Kush and the Indus River (today's Pakistan) was the native land of the Afghan tribes. They called this land "Afghanistan" (meaning "land of the Afghans"). The Afghans ruled the rich northern Indian subcontinent with their capital at <a href="/wiki/Delhi" title="Delhi">Delhi</a>. From the 16th to the early 18th century, Afghanistan was disputed between the <a href="/wiki/Safavid_dynasty" title="Safavid dynasty">Safavids</a> of <a href="/wiki/Isfahan" class="mw-redirect" title="Isfahan">Isfahan</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Mughal_Empire" title="Mughal Empire">Mughals</a> of <a href="/wiki/Agra" title="Agra">Agra</a> who had replaced the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lodi_dynasty&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Lodi dynasty (not yet started)">Lodi</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Sur_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Sur Empire (not yet started)">Suri</a> Afghan rulers in India. The Safavids and Mughals occasionally oppressed the native Afghans but at the same time the Afghans used each empire to punish the other. In 1709, the <a href="/wiki/Hotaki_dynasty" title="Hotaki dynasty">Hotaki</a> Afghans rose to power and completely defeated the Persian Empire. Then they marched towards the Mughals of India and nominally defeated them with the help of the Afsharid forces under Nader Shah Afshar. </p>
      <p>In 1747, after Nader Shah of Persia was killed, a great leader named <a href="/wiki/Ahmad_Shah_Durrani" title="Ahmad Shah Durrani">Ahmad Shah Durrani</a> united all the different Muslim tribes and established the Afghan Empire (<a href="/wiki/Durrani_Empire" title="Durrani Empire">Durrani Empire</a>). He is considered the founding father of the modern state of Afghanistan<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-23">[22]</a></sup> while <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mirwais_Hotak&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mirwais Hotak (not yet started)">Mirwais Hotak</a> is the grandfather of the nation. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_history">Recent history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afghanistan&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=9" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Recent history">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afghanistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Change section: Recent history">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>During the 1800s, Afghanistan became a buffer zone between two powerful empires, <a href="/wiki/British_India" title="British India">British India</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russia</a>. As British India advanced into Afghanistan, Russia felt threatened and expanded southward across Central Asia. To stop the Russian advance, Britain tried to make Afghanistan part of its empire but the Afghans fought wars with British-led Indians from 1839 to 1842 and from 1878 to 1880. After the third war in 1919, Afghanistan under <a href="/wiki/Amanullah_Khan" class="mw-redirect" title="Amanullah Khan">King Amanullah</a> gained respect and recognition as a completely independent state. </p>
      <p>The Kingdom of Afghanistan was a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a> established in 1926. It was the successor state to the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Emirate_of_Afghanistan&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Emirate of Afghanistan (not yet started)">Emirate of Afghanistan</a>. On 27 September 1934, during the reign of Zahir Shah, the Kingdom of Afghanistan joined the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a>. During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, Afghanistan remained neutral. It pursued a <a href="/wiki/Diplomacy" title="Diplomacy">diplomatic policy</a> of non-alignment. </p>
      <p>The creation of Pakistan in 1947 as its eastern neighbor created problems. In 1973, political crises led to the overthrow of the king. The country's new leader ended the monarchy and made Afghanistan a <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a>. In 1978, a <a href="/wiki/Communist" class="mw-redirect" title="Communist">Communist</a> political party supported by the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> seized control of Afghanistan's government. This move sparked rebellions throughout the country. The government asked the Soviet Union for military assistance. The Soviets took advantage of the situation and <a href="/wiki/Soviet_war_in_Afghanistan" class="mw-redirect" title="Soviet war in Afghanistan">invaded Afghanistan in December 1979</a>. </p>
      <p>Most people in Afghanistan opposed the sudden Soviet presence in their country. For nearly a decade, anti-Communist Islamic forces known as <i>Mujahideen</i> were trained inside neighboring Pakistan to fight the Soviets and the Afghan government. The <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> and other anti-Soviet countries supported the Mujahideen. In the long war, over one million Afghan civilians were killed. The Soviet Army also lost more than 15,000 soldiers in that war. Millions of Afghans left their country to stay safe in neighboring Pakistan and Iran. In 1989 the Soviet Army withdrew the last of its troops. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:2011_Afghan_Independence_Day-2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/2011_Afghan_Independence_Day-2.jpg/170px-2011_Afghan_Independence_Day-2.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="113" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/2011_Afghan_Independence_Day-2.jpg/255px-2011_Afghan_Independence_Day-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/2011_Afghan_Independence_Day-2.jpg/340px-2011_Afghan_Independence_Day-2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:2011_Afghan_Independence_Day-2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Former <a href="/wiki/President_of_Afghanistan" title="President of Afghanistan">Afghan President</a> <a href="/wiki/Hamid_Karzai" title="Hamid Karzai">Hamid Karzai</a> at the 2011 Afghan Independence Day in <a href="/wiki/Kabul" title="Kabul">Kabul</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>After the Soviets left, different Afghan warlords began fighting for control of the country. The warlords received support from other countries, including neighboring Pakistan and Iran. A very conservative <a href="/wiki/Islamic" class="mw-redirect" title="Islamic">Islamic</a> group known as the <a href="/wiki/Taliban" title="Taliban">Taliban</a> emerged in an attempt to end the civil war. By the late 1990s the Taliban had gained control over 95% of Afghanistan. A group known as the Northern Alliance, based in northern Afghanistan near the border with Tajikistan, continued to fight against the Taliban. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Afghan_soldiers.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Afghan_soldiers.jpg/220px-Afghan_soldiers.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Afghan_soldiers.jpg/330px-Afghan_soldiers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Afghan_soldiers.jpg/440px-Afghan_soldiers.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2100" data-file-height="1500"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Afghan_soldiers.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>-trained <a href="/w/index.php?title=Afghan_National_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Afghan National Army (not yet started)">Afghan National Army</a> (ANA).
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Military_terminal_at_Kabul_International_Airport.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Military_terminal_at_Kabul_International_Airport.jpg/170px-Military_terminal_at_Kabul_International_Airport.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="128" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Military_terminal_at_Kabul_International_Airport.jpg/255px-Military_terminal_at_Kabul_International_Airport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Military_terminal_at_Kabul_International_Airport.jpg/340px-Military_terminal_at_Kabul_International_Airport.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Military_terminal_at_Kabul_International_Airport.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>NATO's military terminal at <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kabul_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kabul International Airport (not yet started)">Kabul International Airport</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Taliban ruled Afghanistan according to their strict version of <a href="/wiki/Islamic_law" class="mw-redirect" title="Islamic law">Islamic law</a>. People whom the Taliban believed violated these laws were given cruel punishments. In addition, the Taliban completely restricted the rights of women. Because of such policies, most countries refused to recognize the Taliban government. Only <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a> (UAE) accepted them as the official government. </p>
      <p>The Taliban also angered other countries by allowing suspected <a href="/wiki/Terrorist" class="mw-redirect" title="Terrorist">terrorists</a> to live freely in Afghanistan. Among them were <a href="/wiki/Osama_bin_Laden" title="Osama bin Laden">Osama bin Laden</a> and members of the <a href="/wiki/Al-Qaeda" title="Al-Qaeda">al-Qaeda</a> terrorist network. In September 2001, the United States blamed bin Laden for the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">terrorist attacks on the World Trade Center in New York City and the Pentagon outside Washington, D.C.</a> The Taliban refused to hand him over to the United States. In response, the United States and its allies launched a bombing campaign against al-Qaeda in October 2001. Within months the Taliban abandoned Kabul, and a new government led by <a href="/wiki/Hamid_Karzai" title="Hamid Karzai">Hamid Karzai</a> came to power, but fighting between the Taliban and US-led armies continued. Taliban fighters have gone into Afghanistan from neighboring Pakistan. Afghans accuse Pakistan's military of being behind the Taliban militants but Pakistan has rejected this and stated that a stable Afghanistan is in Pakistan's own interest. </p>
      <p>In December 2004, Hamid Karzai became the first <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democratically</a> elected president of Afghanistan.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-13">[12]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> began rebuilding Afghanistan, including its military and government institutions. Many schools and colleges were built. Freedom for women has improved. Women can study, work, drive, and run for office. Many Afghan women work as politicians, some are ministers while at least one is a mayor. Others have opened businesses, or joined the military or police. Afghanistan's economy has also improved dramatically, and NATO agreed in 2012 to help the country for at least another 10 years after 2014. In the meantime, Afghanistan improved diplomatic ties with many countries in the world and continues. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afghanistan&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=10" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Government">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afghanistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Change section: Government">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>Afghanistan is a newly formed <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democracy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[37]</a></sup> Under the new <a href="/wiki/Constitution" title="Constitution">constitution</a>, the <a href="/wiki/President" title="President">president</a> and two <a href="/wiki/Vice_president" title="Vice president">vice presidents</a> are elected every five years.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup> The <a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Security_Force_Assistance&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="International Security Force Assistance (not yet started)">International Security Force Assistance</a> (ISAF) helps the government maintain peace and rebuild the country. </p>
      <p>The government still faces problems with the <a href="/wiki/Taliban" title="Taliban">Taliban</a>, internal security, and public services. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Provinces">Provinces</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afghanistan&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=11" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Provinces">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afghanistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Change section: Provinces">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>As of 2004, there are thirty-four <a href="/wiki/Province" title="Province">provinces</a>. Each province is divided into districts. (For cities see <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Afghanistan" title="List of cities in Afghanistan">List of cities in Afghanistan</a>.) </p>

Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2012-07-01</span></span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Abdul+Hai+Habibi&amp;rft.atitle=Afghan+and+Afghanistan&amp;rft.date=1969&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.alamahabibi.com%2FEnglish%2520Articles%2FAfghan_and_Afghanistan.htm&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fsimple.wikipedia.org%3AAfghanistan" class="Z3988"></span></span> </li>

Brill<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2010-10-22</span></span>. <q><i>In pre-Islamic and early Islamic times, the term “Khurassan” frequently had a much wider denotation, covering also parts of what are now Soviet Central Asia and Afghanistan; early Islamic usage often regarded everywhere east of western Persia, sc. Djibal or what was subsequently termed 'Irak 'Adjami, as being included in a vast and ill-defined region of Khurasan, which might even extend to the Indus Valley and Sind.</i></q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=%22Khurasan%22%2C+The+Encyclopaedia+of+Islam%2C+page+55.&amp;rft.pub=Brill&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DcJQ3AAAAIAAJ%26printsec%3Dfrontcover%23v%3Donepage%26q%26f%3Dfalse&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fsimple.wikipedia.org%3AAfghanistan" class="Z3988"></span></span> </li> 
        <li id="cite_note-Britannica-35"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-Britannica_35-0">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text">
          <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r7263714"><cite class="citation web cs1"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.britannica.com/EBchecked/topic/316850/Khorasan">"Khorasan"</a>. Encyclopædia Britannica Online<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2010-10-21</span></span>. <q><i>historical region and realm comprising a vast territory now lying in northeastern Iran, southern Turkmenistan, and northern Afghanistan. The historical region extended, along the north, from the Amu Darya (Oxus River) westward to the Caspian Sea and, along the south, from the fringes of the central Iranian deserts eastward to the mountains of central Afghanistan. Arab geographers even spoke of its extending to the boundaries of <a href="/wiki/Hindustan" class="mw-disambig" title="Hindustan">India</a>.</i></q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Khorasan&amp;rft.pub=Encyclop%C3%A6dia+Britannica+Online&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.britannica.com%2FEBchecked%2Ftopic%2F316850%2FKhorasan&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fsimple.wikipedia.org%3AAfghanistan" class="Z3988"></span></span> </li>

          <td class="navbox-abovebelow" colspan="2">
           <div>
            <small>1. Includes territory in both <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>. 2. Usually thought of <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> for <a href="/wiki/Culture" title="Culture">cultural</a>, <a href="/wiki/Politics" title="Politics">political</a> and <a href="/wiki/History" title="History">historical</a> reasons. 3. Special territories. 4. Disputed territories.</small>
